style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background-color: #efefef; padding:0.15em 0.25em 0.5em;">Notable <a href="/wiki/Economist" title="Economist">economists</a></div><div class="NavContent navbox-abovebelow" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;background-color: #ffffff;"><div class="hlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Quesnay" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Quesnay">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Quesnay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/David_Ricardo" title="David Ricardo">David Ricardo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Robert_Malthus" title="Thomas Marx</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Walras" title="L\xc3\xa9on Walras">L\xc3\xa9on Walras</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Marshall" title="Alfred Marshall">Alfred Marshall</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">John Maynard Keynes</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Cecil_Pigou" title="Arthur Cecil Pigou">Arthur Cecil Pigou</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Samuelson" title="Paul Samuelson">Paul Samuelson</a></li></ul>\n</div></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background-color: #efefef; padding:0.15em 0.25em 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Category:Economics_lists" title="Category:Economics lists">Lists</a></div><div class="NavContent navbox-abovebelow" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;background-color: #ffffff;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_economists" title="List of economists">Economists</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_important_publications_in_economics" title="List of important publications in economics">Publications</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/List_of_economics_journals" title="List of economics journals">journals</a>)</li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background-color: #efefef; padding:0.15em 0.25em 0.5em;">Glossary</div><div class="NavContent navbox-abovebelow" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;background-color: #ffffff;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_economics" title="Glossary of economics">Glossary of economics</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td class="navbox-abovebelow" style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;background-color: #efefef;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem-money.svg" class="image"><img alt="Emblem-money.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/16px-Emblem-money.svg.png" width="16" height="16" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/24px-Emblem-money.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/32px-Emblem-money.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Business_and_economics" title="Portal:Business and economics">Business and economics&#32;portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Economics_sidebar" title="Template:Economics sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Economics_sidebar" title="Template talk:Economics sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Economics_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</b> (<b>OECD</b>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Organisation de coop\xc3\xa9ration et de d\xc3\xa9veloppement \xc3\xa9conomiques</i>, <i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">OCDE</i></i>) is an <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental economic organisation</a> with 36&#160;member countries,<sup id="cite_ref-membership_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-membership-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> founded in 1961 to stimulate economic progress and world trade. It is a forum of countries describing themselves as committed to <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, providing a platform to compare policy experiences, seeking answers to common problems, identify good practices and coordinate domestic and international policies of its members. Most OECD members are <a href="/wiki/High_income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High income economy">high-income economies</a> with a very high <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) and are regarded as <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed countries</a>. As of 2017, the OECD member states collectively comprised 62.2% of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">global nominal GDP</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>49.6 trillion)<sup id="cite_ref-GDP_IMF_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP_IMF-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and 42.8% of global GDP (<a href="/wiki/Geary%E2%80%93Khamis_dollar" title="Geary\xe2\x80\x93Khamis dollar">Int$</a>54.2 trillion) at <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">purchasing power parity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-imf1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> OECD is an official <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">United Nations observer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1948, the OECD originated as the Organisation for European Economic Co-operation (OEEC),<sup id="cite_ref-oeec_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oeec-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> led by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Marjolin" title="Robert Marjolin">Robert Marjolin</a> of France, to help administer the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> (which was rejected by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Satellite_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Satellite states">satellite states</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> This would be achieved by allocating United States financial aid and implementing economic programs for the reconstruction of Europe after World War&#160;II. (Similar reconstruction aid was sent to the war-torn <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912\xe2\x80\x931949)">Republic of China</a> and post-war Korea, but not under the name "Marshall Plan".)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1961, the OEEC was reformed into the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development by the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Convention on the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Convention on the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> and membership was extended to non-European states.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>  The OECD\'s headquarters are at the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_la_Muette" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teau de la Muette">Ch\xc3\xa2teau de la Muette</a> in Paris, France.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The OECD is funded by contributions from member states at varying rates and had a total budget of \xe2\x82\xac374&#160;million in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-budget_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-budget-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toctext">Structure</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Meetings"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Meetings</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Secretariat"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Secretariat</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Committees"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Committees</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Special_bodies_and_entities[49]"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Special bodies and entities<sup>&#91;49&#93;</sup></span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Member_countries"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Member countries</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Current_members"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Current members</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Former_members"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Former members</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Countries_signed_accession_agreement_but_not_members_yet"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span under consideration by the OECD Council</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Indicators"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Indicators</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_for_European_Economic_Co-operation">Organisation for European Economic Co-operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Organisation for European Economic Co-operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <b>Organisation for European Economic Co-operation</b> (<b>OEEC</b>) was formed in 1948 to administer American and Canadian aid in the framework of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> for the reconstruction of Europe after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-warren_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warren-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It started its operations on 16 April 1948, and originated from the work done by the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_European_Economic_Co-operation" title="Committee of European Economic Co-operation">Committee of European Economic Co-operation</a> in 1947 in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a>. Since 1949, it was headquartered in the Ch\xc3\xa2teau de la Muette in Paris, France. After the Marshall Plan ended, the OEEC focused on economic issues.<sup id="cite_ref-oeec_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oeec-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1950s, the OEEC provided the framework for negotiations aimed at determining conditions for setting up a <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="European Free Trade Area">European Free Trade Area</a>, to bring the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> of the six and the other OEEC members together on a multilateral basis. In 1958, a <a href="/wiki/European_Nuclear_Energy_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="European Nuclear Energy Agency">European Nuclear Energy Agency</a> was set up under the OEEC.\n</p><p>By the end of the 1950s, with the job of rebuilding Europe effectively done, some leading countries felt that the OEEC had outlived its purpose, but could be adapted to fulfill a more global mission. It would be a hard-fought task, and after several sometimes fractious meetings at the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Majestic_(Paris)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hotel Majestic (Paris)">Hotel Majestic</a> in Paris starting in January 1960, a resolution was reached to create a body that would deal not only with European and Atlantic economic issues, but devise policies to assist less developed countries. This reconstituted organisation would bring the US and Canada, who were already OEEC observers, on board as full members. It would also set to work straight away on bringing in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Founding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the 1957 <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaties of Rome">Rome Treaties</a> to launch the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Convention on the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Convention on the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> was drawn up to reform the OEEC. The Convention was signed in December 1960 and the OECD officially superseded the OEEC in September 1961. It consisted of the European founder countries of the OEEC plus the United States and Canada, with Japan joining three years later. The official founding members are:\n</p>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:72%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li>Austria</li>\n<li>Belgium</li>\n<li>Canada</li>\n<li>Denmark</li>\n<li>France</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li>West Germany</li>\n<li>Greece</li>\n<li>Iceland</li>\n<li>Ireland</li>\n<li>Italy</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li>Luxembourg</li>\n<li>The Netherlands</li>\n<li>Norway</li>\n<li>Portugal</li>\n<li>Spain</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li>Sweden</li>\n<li>Switzerland</li>\n<li>Turkey</li>\n<li>United Kingdom</li>\n<li>United States</li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>During the next 12 years Japan, Finland, Australia, and New Zealand also joined the organisation. <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> had observer status in the organisation starting with the establishment of the OECD until its dissolution as a country.<sup id="cite_ref-slovenia_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slovenia-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The OECD created agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/OECD_Development_Centre" title="OECD Development Centre">OECD Development Centre</a> (1961), <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> (IEA, 1974), and <a href="/wiki/Financial_Action_Task_Force_on_Money_Laundering" title="Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering">Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering</a>.\n</p><p>Unlike the organisations of the United Nations system, OECD uses the spelling "organisation" with an "s" in its name rather than "organization" (see <a href="/wiki/-ise" class="mw-redirect" title="-ise">-ise</a>/<a href="/wiki/-ize" class="mw-redirect" title="-ize">-ize</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlargement_to_Central_Europe">Enlargement to Central Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Enlargement to Central Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1989, after the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">Revolutions of 1989</a>, the OECD started to assist countries in Central Europe (especially the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegr\xc3\xa1d Group">Visegr\xc3\xa1d Group</a>) to prepare market economy reforms. In 1990, the Centre for Co-operation with European Economies in Transition (now succeeded by the Centre for Cooperation with Non-Members) was established, and in 1991, the Programme "Partners in Transition" was launched for the benefit of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, Hungary, and Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-slovenia_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slovenia-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-czech_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-czech-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> This programme also included a membership option for these countries.<sup id="cite_ref-czech_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-czech-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> As a result of this, Poland,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Hungary, the Czech Republic, and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, as well as Mexico and South Korea<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> became members of the OECD between 1994 and 2000.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reform_and_further_enlargement">Reform and further enlargement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Reform and further enlargement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the 1990s, a number of European countries, now members of the European Union, expressed their willingness to join the organisation. In 1995, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> applied for membership, but, according to the Cypriot government, it was vetoed by <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> signed a Joint Declaration expressing willingness to become full members of the OECD.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> also applied for membership that same year.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> applied to join the organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The EU is lobbying for admission of all <a href="/wiki/EU_member_states" class="mw-redirect" title="EU member states">EU member states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> reaffirmed in 2012 its intention to become a member of the organisation through the letter addressed by the Romanian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Victor_Ponta" title="Victor Ponta">Victor Ponta</a> to OECD Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_%C3%81ngel_Gurr%C3%ADa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 \xc3\x81ngel Gurr\xc3\xada">Jos\xc3\xa9 \xc3\x81ngel Gurr\xc3\xada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In September 2012, the government of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> confirmed it will apply for full membership before the OECD Secretariat.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2003, the OECD established a working group headed by Japan\'s Ambassador to the OECD Seiichiro Noboru to work out a strategy for the enlargement and co-operation with non-members. The working group proposed that the selection of candidate countries to be based on four criteria: "like-mindedness", "significant player", "mutual benefit" and "global considerations". The working group\'s recommendations were presented at the OECD Ministerial Council Meeting on 13 and 14 May 2004. Based on these recommendations work, the meeting adopted an agreement on operationalisation of the proposed guidelines and on the drafting of a list of countries suitable as potential candidates for membership.<sup id="cite_ref-slovenia_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slovenia-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> As a result of this work, on 16 May 2007, the OECD Ministerial Council decided to open accession discussions with <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, Estonia, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, Russia and Slovenia and to strengthen co-operation with <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, China, India, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and South Africa through a process of enhanced engagement.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd2007_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd2007-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Chile, Slovenia, Israel and Estonia all became members in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>  In March 2014, the OECD halted membership talks with Russia in response to its role in the <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Crimean crisis">2014 Crimean crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, the OECD decided to open membership talks with <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and Latvia. In 2015, it opened talks with <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> and Lithuania.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd300513_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd300513-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Latvia became a full member on 1 July 2016 and Lithuania on 5 July 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-leta010716_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leta010716-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vz050718_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vz050718-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Colombia signed the accession agreement on 30 May 2018 and will become full member after the ratification of the accession agreement and the deposition of the ratification document.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd-co-invitation_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-co-invitation-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other countries that have expressed interest in OECD membership are <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Objectives_and_activities">Objectives and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Objectives and activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The OECD publishes and updates a model tax convention that serves as a template for bilateral negotiations regarding tax coordination and cooperation. This model is accompanied by a set of commentaries that reflect OECD-level interpretation of the content of the model convention provisions. In general, this model allocates the primary right to tax to the country from which capital investment originates (i.e., the home, or resident country) rather than the country in which the investment is made (the host, or source country). As a result, it is most effective as between two countries with reciprocal investment flows (such as among the OECD member countries), but can be very unbalanced when one of the signatory countries is economically weaker than the other (such as between OECD and non-OECD pairings).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishing">Publishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Publishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The OECD publishes books, reports, statistics, working papers and reference materials. All titles and databases published since 1998 can be accessed via <a href="/wiki/OECD_iLibrary" title="OECD iLibrary">OECD iLibrary</a>.\n</p><p>The OECD Library &amp; Archives collection dates from 1947, including records from the Committee for European Economic Co-operation (CEEC) and the Organisation for European Economic Co-operation (OEEC), predecessors of today\'s OECD. External researchers can consult OECD publications and archival material on the OECD premises by appointment.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The OECD releases between 300 and 500 books each year. The publications are updated accordingly to the OECD iLibrary. Most books are published in English and French. The OECD flagship<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (September 2013)">vague</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> titles include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Economic_Outlook_(OECD_publication)" title="Economic Outlook (OECD publication)">OECD Economic Outlook</a>, published twice a year. It contains forecast and analysis of the economic situation of the OECD member countries.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/OECD_Main_Economic_Indicators" title="OECD Main Economic Indicators">Main Economic Indicators</a>, published monthly. It contains a large selection of timely statistical indicators.</li>\n<li>The OECD Factbook, published yearly and available online, as an iPhone app and in print. The Factbook contains more than 100 economic, environmental and social indicators, each presented with a clear definition, tables and graphs. The Factbook mainly focuses on the statistics of its member countries and sometimes other major additional countries. It is freely accessible online and delivers all the data in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Excel</a> format via StatLinks.</li>\n<li>The OECD Communications Outlook and the OECD Internet Economy Outlook (formerly the Information Technology Outlook), which rotate every year. They contain forecasts and analysis of the communications and information technology industries in OECD member countries and non-member economies.</li>\n<li>In 2007 the OECD published <i>Human Capital: How what you know shapes your life</i>, the first book in the <i>OECD Insights</i> series. This series uses OECD analysis and data to introduce important social and economic issues to non-specialist readers. Other books in the series cover sustainable development, international trade and international migration.</li></ul>\n<p>All OECD books are available on the OECD iLibrary, the online bookshop or OECD Library &amp; Archives.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazine">Magazine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Magazine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><i>OECD Observer</i>, an award-winning magazine<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;n 2&#93;</a></sup> launched in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The magazine appeared six times a year until 2010, and became quarterly in 2011 with the introduction of the <i>OECD Yearbook</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;n 3&#93;</a></sup> launched for the 50th anniversary of the organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The online and mobile<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> editions are updated regularly. News, analysis, reviews, commentaries and data on global economic, social and environmental challenges. Contains listing of the latest OECD books, plus ordering information.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> An OECD Observer Crossword was introduced in Q2 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The OECD is known as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_and_international_statistical_services" title="List of national and international statistical services">statistical agency</a>, as it publishes comparable statistics on a wide number of subjects.\n</p><p>OECD statistics are available in several forms:\n</p>\n<ul><li>as interactive databases on iLibrary together with key comparative and country tables,</li>\n<li>as static files or dynamic database views on the OECD Statistics portal,</li>\n<li>as StatLinks (in most OECD books, there is a <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Locator" class="mw-redirect" title="Uniform Resource Locator">URL</a> that links to the underlying data).</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Working_papers">Working papers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Working papers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>There are 15 working papers series published by the various directorates of the OECD Secretariat. They are available on iLibrary, as well as on many specialised portals.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reference_works">Reference works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Reference works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The OECD is responsible for the <a href="/wiki/OECD_Guidelines_for_the_Testing_of_Chemicals" title="OECD Guidelines for the Testing of Chemicals">OECD Guidelines for the Testing of Chemicals</a>, a continuously updated document that is a <i>de facto</i> standard (i.e., soft law).\n</p><p>It has published the <i>OECD Environmental Outlook to 2030</i>, which shows that tackling the key environmental problems we face today\xe2\x80\x94including <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">biodiversity loss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">water scarcity</a>, and the health impacts of <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>\xe2\x80\x94is both achievable and affordable.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The OECD\'s structure consists of three main elements:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The OECD <a href="#Member_countries">member countries</a>, each represented by a delegation led by an ambassador. Together, they form the OECD Council. Member countries act collectively through Council (and its Standing Committees) to provide direction and guidance to the work of Organisation.</li>\n<li>The OECD Substantive <a href="/wiki/OECD#Committees" title="OECD">Committees</a>, one for each work area of the OECD, plus their variety of subsidiary bodies. Committee members are typically subject-matter experts from member and non-member governments. The Committees oversee all the work on each theme (publications, task forces, conferences, and so on). Committee members then relay the conclusions to their capitals.</li>\n<li>The OECD <a href="/wiki/OECD#Secretariat" title="OECD">Secretariat</a>, led by the Secretary-General (currently <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Gurr%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x81ngel Gurr\xc3\xada">\xc3\x81ngel Gurr\xc3\xada</a>), provides support to Standing and Substantive Committees. It is organised into Directorates, which include about 2,500 staff.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meetings">Meetings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Meetings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dd/Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg/220px-Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dd/Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg/330px-Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dd/Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg/440px-Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3664" data-file-height="2748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_the_OECD_Conference_Centre_April_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main entrance to the OECD Conference Centre in Paris</div></div></div>\n<p>Delegates from the member countries attend committees\' and other meetings. Former <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary General">Deputy Secretary-General</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Vinde&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pierre Vinde (page does not exist)">Pierre Vinde</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://sv.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Vinde" class="extiw" title="sv:Pierre Vinde">sv</a>)</span> estimated in 1997 that the cost borne by the member countries, such as sending their officials to OECD meetings and maintaining permanent delegations, is equivalent to the cost of running the secretariat.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> This ratio is unique among inter-governmental organisations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In other words, the OECD is more a persistent forum or network of officials and experts than an administration.\n</p><p>The OECD regularly holds minister-level meetings and forums as platforms for a discussion on a broad spectrum of thematic issues relevant to the OECD charter, members and non-member states.<sup id="cite_ref-OECDforums_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECDforums-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Noteworthy meetings include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The yearly Ministerial Council Meeting, with the Ministers of Economy of all member countries and the candidates for enhanced engagement among the countries.</li>\n<li>The annual OECD Forum, which brings together leaders from business, government, labour, civil society and international organisations. Held every year since June 2000, the OECD Forum takes the form of conferences and discussions, is open to public participation and is held in conjunction with the MCM.</li>\n<li>Thematic Ministerial Meetings, held among Ministers of a given domain (i.e., all Ministers of Labour, all Ministers of Environment, etc.).</li>\n<li>The bi-annual World Forum on Statistics, Knowledge and Policies, which does not usually take place in the OECD. This series of meetings has the ambition to measure and foster progress in societies.</li>\n<li>OECD Eurasia Week which includes several high-level policy dialogue discussions to share best practices and experiences in addressing common development and economic challenges in Eurasia.<sup id="cite_ref-EurasiaWk_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurasiaWk-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secretariat">Secretariat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Secretariat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Exchanges between OECD governments benefit from the information, analysis, and preparation of the OECD Secretariat. The secretariat collects data, monitors trends, and analyses and forecasts economic developments. Under the direction and guidance of member governments, it also researches social changes or evolving patterns in trade, environment, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, technology, <a href="/wiki/Tax" title="Tax">taxation</a>, and other areas.\n</p><p>The secretariat is organised in Directorates:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Centre for Entrepreneurship, <a href="/wiki/Small_and_Medium_Enterprises" class="mw-redirect" title="Small and Medium Enterprises">Small and Medium Enterprises</a> (SMEs) and Local Development</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Tax_Policy_and_Administration" title="Centre for Tax Policy and Administration">Centre for Tax Policy and Administration</a></li>\n<li>Development Co-operation Directorate</li>\n<li>Directorate for Education and Skills</li>\n<li>Directorate for Employment, Labour, and Social Affairs</li>\n<li>Directorate for Financial and Enterprise Affairs</li>\n<li>Directorate for Science, Technology, and Innovation</li>\n<li>Economics Department</li>\n<li>Environment Directorate</li>\n<li>Public Governance Directorate</li>\n<li>Statistics Directorate</li>\n<li>Trade and Agriculture Directorate</li>\n<li>General Secretariat</li>\n<li>Executive Directorate</li>\n<li>Public Affairs and Communication Directorate</li></ul>\n<table class="wikitable" style="clear:right; text-align:center">\n<caption>Secretary-General of the France\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Thorkil_Kristensen" title="Thorkil Kristensen">Thorkil Kristensen</a>\n</td>\n<td>1960 \xe2\x80\x93 September 1961\n</td>\n<td><span href="http://www.oecd.org/about/secretary-general/listofoecdsecretaries-generalanddeputiessince1961.htm">source</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Committees">Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Representatives of member and observer countries meet in specialised committees on specific policy areas, such as economics, trade, science, employment, education or financial markets. There are about 200&#160;committees, working groups and expert groups. Committees discuss policies and review progress in the given policy area.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Special_bodies_and_entities.5B49.5D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_bodies_and_entities[49]">Special bodies and entities<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a (BIAC)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Development_Assistance_Committee" title="Development Assistance Committee">Development Assistance Committee</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/OECD_Development_Centre" class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Countries currently in accession talks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Costa Rica: In May 2013, the OECD declared its intention to open accession negotiations with Costa Rica in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> On 9 April 2015, the OECD decided to open accession negotiations with Costa Rica.<sup id="cite_ref-crlneg_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crlneg-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_whose_accession_talks_are_suspended">Countries whose accession talks are suspended</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=OECD&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Countries whose accession talks are suspended">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Russia: In May 2007, the OECD decided to open accession negotiations with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd2007_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd2007-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In March 2014, the OECD halted membership talks in response to Russia\'s role in href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span
